{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}1}]:} \PY{o}{\PYZpc{}}\PY{k}{matplotlib} \PY{n}{inline}
\end{Verbatim}

    Calculations of distributions of proplyd distances and sizes and angles.
These translate into distributions of $\beta$.

    \subsection{Data sources}\label{data-sources}

We have the list of proplyds from Henney \& Arthur (1998) that we used
in Fig 12 of Tsamis et al (2013). This has distances and sizes.

We also have the Ricci et al (2008) catalog, which has distances but not
sizes.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

          \PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n+nn}{seaborn} \PY{k+kn}{as} \PY{n+nn}{sns}
          \PY{k+kn}{from} \PY{n+nn}{scipy} \PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n}{stats}
\end{Verbatim}

    Now use seaborn to get nicer graphs.

    We need to take account of binaries

    Now we will try out some of the seaborn tools for visualizing data
distributions. See
\href{http://web.stanford.edu/~mwaskom/software/seaborn/tutorial/plotting_distributions.html}{this
tutorial}.

    In the section on the Ricci data it occured to me that we need to mirror
the data about zero because the radius and separation are
positive-definite.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

    The simplest option is \texttt{boxplot}, which shows the median and
quartiles. By setting \texttt{whis=np.inf} we make the whiskers extend
out to the full range of the data.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{ylabel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Proplyd size, 1e14 cm}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{xlabel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Projected distance band}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n+nb+bp}{None}

    \adjustimage{max size={0.9\linewidth}{0.9\paperheight}}{Proplyd distribution_files/Proplyd distribution_25_0.png}
    \end{center}
    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    Alternatively we can use \texttt{violinplot}, which shows the Kernel
Density Estimate (KDE) of the values in each category. By setting
\texttt{inner="points"} it shows the actual data points instead of the
quartiles.

I am a little uncomfortable of this way of presenting the data, since we
are forcing the distance to be categorical, when really it is
continuous.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}421}]:} \PY{n}{sns}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{violinplot}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{mirrored\PYZus{}datalist}\PY{p}{,} 
                         \PY{n}{names}\PY{o}{=}\PY{n}{namelist}\PY{p}{,}
                         \PY{n}{inner}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{points}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{bw}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+m+mf}{0.3}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{color}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{PuBuGn}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{ylim}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mf}{0.0}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n+nb+bp}{None}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{ylabel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Proplyd size, 1e14 cm}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{xlabel}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Projected distance band}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n+nb+bp}{None}
\end{Verbatim}

    \begin{center}
    \adjustimage{max size={0.9\linewidth}{0.9\paperheight}}{Proplyd distribution_files/Proplyd distribution_27_0.png}
    \end{center}
    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}422}]:} \PY{n}{sns}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{jointplot}\PY{err}{?}
\end{Verbatim}

    Try it again, but non-cumulative. If the cumulative distribution is
linear in $D'$ then the non-cumulative one should be constant.

    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    The ultimate tool for plotting a distribution is \texttt{distplot}. This
can show the following if we turn on all the options: 1. A rugplot of
the individual data points 2. A histogram of the distribution 3. The KDE
of the distribution 4. A fit to the distribution of any function from
\texttt{scipy.stats}

    \adjustimage{max size={0.9\linewidth}{0.9\paperheight}}{Proplyd distribution_files/Proplyd distribution_51_0.png}
    \end{center}
    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    What I don't like about this is that the KDE is affected by the fact
that there are no points with $D' < 0$. That is why it drops towards
zero. To fix this, we could reflect the dataset about zero and add a
negative mirrored dataset.

Note that \texttt{stats.laplace} is actually a 2-sided explonential. And
it doesn't fit very well. On the other hand, the KDE now looks much
nicer.

    So now, we will try the same trick on the joint distribution of $D'$ and
$r_0$. This is in a previous section.

    Zooming in on the central part, which is relevant to the bowshocks.

                       \PY{n}{fit\PYZus{}kws}\PY{o}{=}\PY{p}{\PYZob{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{label}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Constant fit}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{p}{,}
                       \PY{n}{hist\PYZus{}kws}\PY{o}{=}\PY{p}{\PYZob{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{range}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{:} \PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{\PYZhy{}}\PY{n}{Dmaxx}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{Dmaxx}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{\PYZcb{}}\PY{p}{,}
                       \PY{n}{bins}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+m+mi}{2}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{Dmaxx}\PY{o}{/}\PY{o}{/}\PY{l+m+mi}{10}\PY{p}{,}
                       \PY{n}{label}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Histogram (10 arcsec bins)}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{axlabel}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+s}{r\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Projected distance, \PYZdl{}D}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdl{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{legend}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{loc}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{upper left}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{xlim}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+m+mf}{0.0}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+m+mf}{100.0}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{plt}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{title}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{Distribution of projected distances for all bright proplyds from Ricci et al. (2008) sample}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{;}
\end{Verbatim}

    \begin{center}
    \adjustimage{max size={0.9\linewidth}{0.9\paperheight}}{Proplyd distribution_files/Proplyd distribution_56_0.png}
    \end{center}
    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    So this suggests that at scales $< 100''$ the proplyd distribution is
uniform (implying density $\sim D^{-2}$.

Whereas at larger scales it does fall off.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}532}]:} \PY{n}{sns}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{kdeplot}\PY{err}{?}
\end{Verbatim}

    We first need to restrict the table to unique sources, since it contains
multiple observations of the same source. We can do this by comparing
the first two columns:

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}23}]:} \PY{n}{m\PYZus{}uniq} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{Seq}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{oncacs}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}
\end{Verbatim}

    Then winnowing down the table:

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}24}]:} \PY{n}{sdata} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{m\PYZus{}uniq}\PY{p}{]}
\end{Verbatim}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}24}]:} 
\end{Verbatim}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}24}]:} 
\end{Verbatim}

    Description of the \texttt{type} column from notes to Table 5:

\begin{verbatim}
Source type, from visual inspection: (0) not measured; (1) detected in at least one filter and unresolved; (2) double (companion closer than ≈3 pixels, one entry for both sources); (3) wide double (companion further than ≈3 pixel, one entry for each source); (5) silhouette disk; (6) photoionized (proplyd or with other evidence of photoionization); (7) galaxy; (8) Herbig-Haro.
\end{verbatim}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}25}]:} \PY{n}{source\PYZus{}types} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{not measured}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{single}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{close double}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{wide double}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} 
                         \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{???}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{disk}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{ionized}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{galaxy}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{herbig haro}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}

             \PY{n}{count\PYZus{}table}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{add\PYZus{}row}\PY{p}{(}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{itype}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{label}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{sum}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{type}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{n}{itype}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
         \PY{n}{count\PYZus{}table}
\end{Verbatim}

            \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{outcolor}Out[{\color{outcolor}25}]:} <Table rows=9 names=('Code','Type','Number')>
         array([(0, b'not measured', 2), (1, b'single', 2912),
                (2, b'close double', 47), (3, b'wide double', 154), (4, b'???', 0),
                (5, b'disk', 36), (6, b'ionized', 184), (7, b'galaxy', 59),

    The \texttt{ionized} type is ``\emph{proplyd or with other evidence of
photoionization}'' and there are 184 of them, compared with 178 in the
Ricci catalog. This is close enough for me.

    Next job is to winnow out types 0, 7, and 8, which we don't want.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}26}]:} \PY{n}{sdata} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{type}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{\PYZgt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{0}\PY{p}{)} \PY{o}{\PYZam{}} \PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{type}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{\PYZlt{}} \PY{l+m+mi}{7}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}
\end{Verbatim}

    And now create a mask to select out the \texttt{ionized} sources (mainly
proplyds).

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}27}]:} \PY{n}{m\PYZus{}rob\PYZus{}ionized} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{type}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+m+mi}{6}
\end{Verbatim}

    Now we combine the 6 columns used for coordinates into a single RA-Dec
string:

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}28}]:} \PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{coordstring}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZob{}\PYZcb{} \PYZob{}\PYZcb{} \PYZob{}\PYZcb{} \PYZhy{}\PYZob{}\PYZcb{} \PYZob{}\PYZcb{} \PYZob{}\PYZcb{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{format}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{*}\PY{n}{args}\PY{p}{)}
                           \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{args} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{n+nb}{zip}\PY{p}{(}\PY{o}{*}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{sdata}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{col}\PY{p}{]} \PY{k}{for} \PY{n}{col} \PY{o+ow}{in} \PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{RAh}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{RAm}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{RAs}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{DEd}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{DEm}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{l+s}{DEs}\PY{l+s}{\PYZdq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}\PY{p}{]}
\end{Verbatim}

\end{Verbatim}

          \PY{n}{ax}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{set\PYZus{}title}\PY{p}{(}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{A title}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}

\texttt{\color{outcolor}Out[{\color{outcolor}108}]:}
    
    \begin{center}
    \adjustimage{max size={0.9\linewidth}{0.9\paperheight}}{Proplyd distribution_files/Proplyd distribution_100_0.png}
    \end{center}
    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    

    So the conclusion of this section is that the Ricci proplyd catalog
(shown by blue circles on the image above) is more reliable than the
Robberto \texttt{ionized} catalog (shown by orange circles) for the
close-in proplyds. Robberto is missing a lot of obvious proplyds, and
furthermore has a few sources that don't seem to correspond to anything,
although some might be bowshocks or jet knots.

The Ricci catalog is only missing a very few, such as the one very close
to th1c.

    \subsection{Monte Carlo simulations}\label{monte-carlo-simulations}

Assume power law distribution in radius.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

    { \hspace*{\fill} \\}
    
    \subsubsection{Compare the projected separation and the inclination for
the inner 30 arcsec of the MC
sample}\label{compare-the-projected-separation-and-the-inclination-for-the-inner-30-arcsec-of-the-mc-sample}

Assume that the inner wind shock lies at about $D = 26''$. Only proplyds
that are physically clser than this will have Type I bowshocks. These
are shown by orange points in the figure. Physically more distant
proplyds are shown by gray points. We also show contours of physical
separation every $10''$ from $D = 10''$ to $D = 200''$.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

    Create \texttt{coord.SkyCoord} objects for the two ends of the chord
that I measured at the back of each proplyd's head. Then use those to
find the chord diameter in arcsec (\texttt{Chord} column), and then
convert to a radius in units of $10^{14}$ cm (\texttt{r14} column).

    Take the average of the RA and DEC components of the two ends of the
chord to get an average coordinate (\texttt{coords0}) for each source.
\textbf{Note: This will not quite be the center of the proplyd, but it
is close enough.}

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]

          \PY{n}{coords0}\PY{p}{[}\PY{p}{:}\PY{l+m+mi}{4}\PY{p}{]}

    \begin{center}\rule{3in}{0.4pt}\end{center}

Now we try and merge in the HA98 table.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}747}]:} \PY{k+kn}{from} \PY{n+nn}{astropy.table} \PY{k+kn}{import} \PY{n}{join}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{Column}
\end{Verbatim}

    First naive attempt was a straight outer join on the \texttt{ID} column.
This gave some objects that are in the HA98 table but not in the new
data. Of these, 244-440 is OK, since it is outside our distance cut-off,
but the others need fixing. 177-341 (not in Ricci catalog) is just a
matter of the name, which should be 177-341W. There were also two really
missing: 171-334 and 154-324 (my typo).

So we need to fix things up. First make the \texttt{ID} field in the
HA98 table wider and fix the name of 177-341W.

\emph{This took much longer than it should have done. It turns out that
you can't change the dtype of a column without making a new table}.

    \begin{Verbatim}[commandchars=\\\{\}]
{\color{incolor}In [{\color{incolor}798}]:} \PY{n}{data} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{Table}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{data}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{names}\PY{o}{=}\PY{n}{data}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{colnames}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{dtype}\PY{o}{=}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZlt{}U12}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZlt{}f8}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZlt{}f8}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{,} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZlt{}f8}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{data}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{ID}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{Column}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{data}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{ID}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{,} \PY{n}{dtype}\PY{o}{=}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{\PYZlt{}U12}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{irow} \PY{o}{=} \PY{n}{np}\PY{o}{.}\PY{n}{argmax}\PY{p}{(}\PY{n}{data}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{ID}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{==} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{177\PYZhy{}341}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{)}
          \PY{n}{data}\PY{p}{[}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{ID}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{p}{]}\PY{p}{[}\PY{n}{irow}\PY{p}{]} \PY{o}{=} \PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}\PY{l+s}{177\PYZhy{}341W}\PY{l+s}{\PYZsq{}}

\end{Verbatim}

    And here are the cases where HA98 sizes were more than 30\% smaller.
These are mainly small sized. In this case, I think that the current
results are more reliable because in HA98 we did not remove the central
stars and so overestimated the compactness of some of the small
proplyds.

agreement to a level of about 30\%. This is not bad, given that the
sizes range over an order of magnitude.
